I've uploaded a code repository in the directory . Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
`SmithyIdlSerializer` always renders idRefs unquoted
When serializing a model with an `@idRef` String shape, the `SmithyIdlSerializer` will always render the ShapeId unquoted.

This causes problems when loading the serialized model, because the shape may or may not exist (if `failWhenMissing` isn't used, this isn't a problem beforehand).

For example:

```smithy
$version: "2"

namespace test

@trait structure myTrait { @idRef @required s: String }

@myTrait(s: "foo.bar#Baz") string Demo
```

Becomes:

```smithy
namespace test

use foo.bar#Baz

@trait
structure myTrait {
    @idRef
    @required
    s: String
}

@myTrait(
    s: Baz
)
string Demo
```

which gets rejected when loading:

```
software.amazon.smithy.model.validation.ValidatedResultException: Result contained ERROR severity validation events: 
[DANGER] -: Syntactic shape ID `Baz` does not resolve to a valid shape ID: `foo.bar#Baz`. Did you mean to quote this string? Are you missing a model file? | SyntacticShapeIdTarget test.smithy:15:8
```

Full reproduction in scala-cli:

```scala
//> using scala 3.5.2
//> using dep software.amazon.smithy:smithy-model:1.53.0
//> using option -Wunused:all
import software.amazon.smithy.model.Model
import scala.jdk.CollectionConverters._
import software.amazon.smithy.model.shapes.SmithyIdlModelSerializer

val r = Model
  .assembler()
  .addUnparsedModel(
    "test.smithy",
    """$version: "2"
      |namespace test
      |
      |@trait structure myTrait { @idRef @required s: String }
      |
      |@myTrait(s: "foo.bar#Baz") string Demo
      |""".stripMargin,
  )
  .assemble()

r.getValidationEvents().asScala.toList

val m = r.unwrap()

val srcAgain = SmithyIdlModelSerializer.builder().build().serialize(m).asScala.toList.head._2

Model
  .assembler()
  .addUnparsedModel(
    "test.smithy",
    srcAgain,
  )
  .assemble()
  .unwrap()
```

</pr_description>

    82	         * @param haystack Array of enums to check.
    83	         * @return Returns true if this enum is found in the array.
    84	         */
    85	        boolean hasFeature(TraitFeature[] haystack) {
    86	            for (TraitFeature test : haystack) {
    87	                if (test == this) {
    88	                    return true;
    89	                }
    90	            }
    91	            return false;
    92	        }
    93	    }

    98	        if (builder.serializePrelude) {

   924	    private static final class NodeSerializer {
   925	        private final SmithyCodeWriter codeWriter;
   926	        private final Model model;
   927	
   928	        NodeSerializer(SmithyCodeWriter codeWriter, Model model) {
   929	            this.codeWriter = codeWriter;
   930	            this.model = model;
   931	        }
   932	
   933	        /**
   934	         * Serialize a node into the Smithy IDL format.
   935	         *
   936	         * @param node The node to serialize.
   937	         */
   938	        private void serialize(Node node) {
   939	            serialize(node, null);
   940	        }
   941	
   942	        /**
   943	         * Serialize a node into the Smithy IDL format.
   944	         *
   945	         * <p>This uses the given shape to influence serialization. For example, a string shape marked with the idRef
   946	         * trait will be serialized as a shape id rather than a string.
   947	         *
   948	         * @param node The node to serialize.
   949	         * @param shape The shape of the node.
   950	         */
   951	        private void serialize(Node node, Shape shape) {
   952	            // ShapeIds are represented differently than strings, so if a shape looks like it's
   953	            // representing a shapeId we need to serialize it without quotes.
   954	            if (isShapeId(shape)) {
   955	                serializeShapeId(node.expectStringNode());
   956	                return;
   957	            }
   958	
   959	            if (shape != null && shape.isMemberShape()) {
   960	                shape = model.expectShape(shape.asMemberShape().get().getTarget());
   961	            }
   962	
   963	            if (node.isStringNode()) {
   964	                serializeString(node.expectStringNode());
   965	            } else if (node.isNumberNode()) {
   966	                serializeNumber(node.expectNumberNode());
   967	            } else if (node.isBooleanNode()) {
   968	                serializeBoolean(node.expectBooleanNode());
   969	            } else if (node.isNullNode()) {
   970	                serializeNull();
   971	            } else if (node.isArrayNode()) {
   972	                serializeArray(node.expectArrayNode(), shape);
   973	            } else if (node.isObjectNode()) {
   974	                serializeObject(node.expectObjectNode(), shape);
   975	            }
   976	        }
   977	
   978	        private boolean isShapeId(Shape shape) {
   979	            if (shape == null) {
   980	                return false;
   981	            }
   982	            return shape.getMemberTrait(model, IdRefTrait.class).isPresent();
   983	        }
   984	
   985	        private void serializeString(StringNode node) {
   986	            codeWriter.writeInline("$S", node.getValue());
   987	        }
   988	
   989	        private void serializeShapeId(StringNode node) {
   990	            codeWriter.writeInline("$I", node.getValue());
   991	        }
   992	
   993	        private void serializeNumber(NumberNode node) {
   994	            codeWriter.writeInline("$L", node.getValue());
   995	        }
   996	
   997	        private void serializeBoolean(BooleanNode node) {
   998	            codeWriter.writeInline(String.valueOf(node.getValue()));
   999	        }
  1000	
  1001	        private void serializeNull() {
  1002	            codeWriter.writeInline("null");
  1003	        }
  1004	
  1005	        private void serializeArray(ArrayNode node, Shape shape) {
  1006	            if (node.isEmpty()) {
  1007	                codeWriter.writeInline("[]");
  1008	                return;
  1009	            }
  1010	
  1011	            codeWriter.openBlockInline("[");
  1012	
  1013	            // If it's not a collection shape, it'll be a document shape or null
  1014	            Shape member = shape;
  1015	            if (shape instanceof CollectionShape) {
  1016	                member = ((CollectionShape) shape).getMember();
  1017	            }
  1018	
  1019	            for (Node element : node.getElements()) {
  1020	                // Elements will be written inline to enable them being written as values.
  1021	                // So here we need to ensure that they're written on a new line that's properly indented.
  1022	                codeWriter.write("");
  1023	                codeWriter.writeIndent();
  1024	                serialize(element, member);
  1025	            }
  1026	            codeWriter.write("");
  1027	
  1028	            // We want to make sure to close without inserting a newline, as this could itself be a list element
  1029	            //or an object value.
  1030	            codeWriter.closeBlockWithoutNewline("]");
  1031	        }
  1032	
  1033	        private void serializeObject(ObjectNode node, Shape shape) {
  1034	            if (node.isEmpty()) {
  1035	                codeWriter.writeInline("{}");
  1036	                return;
  1037	            }
  1038	
  1039	            codeWriter.openBlockInline("{");
  1040	            serializeKeyValuePairs(node, shape);
  1041	            codeWriter.closeBlockWithoutNewline("}");
  1042	        }
  1043

  1093	    private static final class SmithyCodeWriter extends SimpleCodeWriter {
  1094	        private static final Pattern UNQUOTED_KEY_STRING = Pattern.compile("[a-zA-Z_][a-zA-Z_0-9]*");
  1095	        private final String namespace;
  1096	        private final Model model;
  1097	        private final Set<ShapeId> imports;
  1098	
  1099	        SmithyCodeWriter(String namespace, Model model) {
  1100	            super();
  1101	            this.namespace = namespace;
  1102	            this.model = model;
  1103	            this.imports = new HashSet<>();
  1104	            trimTrailingSpaces();
  1105	            trimBlankLines();
  1106	            putFormatter('I', (s, i) -> formatShapeId(s));
  1107	            putFormatter('K', this::optionallyQuoteKey);
  1108	        }
  1109	
  1110	        /**
  1111	         * Opens a block without writing indentation whitespace or inserting a newline.
  1112	         */
  1113	        private SmithyCodeWriter openBlockInline(String content, Object... args) {
  1114	            writeInline(content, args).indent();
  1115	            return this;
  1116	        }
  1117	
  1118	        /**
  1119	         * Closes a block without inserting a newline.
  1120	         */
  1121	        private SmithyCodeWriter closeBlockWithoutNewline(String content, Object... args) {
  1122	            setNewline("");
  1123	            closeBlock(content, args);
  1124	            setNewline("\n");
  1125	            return this;
  1126	        }
  1127	
  1128	        /**
  1129	         * Writes an empty line that contains only indentation appropriate to the current indentation level.
  1130	         *
  1131	         * <p> This does not insert a trailing newline.
  1132	         */
  1133	        private SmithyCodeWriter writeIndent() {
  1134	            setNewline("");
  1135	            // We explicitly want the trailing spaces, so disable trimming for this call.
  1136	            trimTrailingSpaces(false);
  1137	            write("");
  1138	            trimTrailingSpaces();
  1139	            setNewline("\n");
  1140	            return this;
  1141	        }
  1142	
  1143	        private String formatShapeId(Object value) {
  1144	            if (value == null) {
  1145	                return "";
  1146	            }
  1147	            ShapeId shapeId = ShapeId.from(String.valueOf(value));
  1148	            if (!shouldWriteNamespace(shapeId)) {
  1149	                return shapeId.asRelativeReference();
  1150	            }
  1151	            return shapeId.toString();
  1152	        }
  1153	
  1154	        private boolean shouldWriteNamespace(ShapeId shapeId) {
  1155	            if (shapeId.getNamespace().equals(namespace)) {
  1156	                return false;
  1157	            }
  1158	            if (Prelude.isPublicPreludeShape(shapeId)) {
  1159	                return conflictsWithLocalNamespace(shapeId);
  1160	            }
  1161	            if (shouldImport(shapeId)) {
  1162	                imports.add(shapeId.withoutMember());
  1163	            }
  1164	            return !imports.contains(shapeId);
  1165	        }
  1166	
  1167	        private boolean conflictsWithLocalNamespace(ShapeId shapeId) {
  1168	            return model.getShape(ShapeId.fromParts(namespace, shapeId.getName())).isPresent();
  1169	        }
  1170	
  1171	        private boolean shouldImport(ShapeId shapeId) {
  1172	            return !conflictsWithLocalNamespace(shapeId)
  1173	                    // It's easier to simply never import something that conflicts with the prelude, because
  1174	                    // if we did then we'd have to somehow handle rewriting all existing references to the
  1175	                    // prelude shape that it conflicts with.
  1176	                    && !conflictsWithPreludeNamespace(shapeId)
  1177	                    && !conflictsWithImports(shapeId);
  1178	
  1179	        }
  1180	
  1181	        private boolean conflictsWithPreludeNamespace(ShapeId shapeId) {
  1182	            return Prelude.isPublicPreludeShape(ShapeId.fromParts(Prelude.NAMESPACE, shapeId.getName()));
  1183	        }
  1184	
  1185	        private boolean conflictsWithImports(ShapeId shapeId) {
  1186	            return imports.stream().anyMatch(importId -> importId.getName().equals(shapeId.getName()));
  1187	        }
  1188	
  1189	        /**
  1190	         * Writes a possibly-empty list where each element is a shape id.
  1191	         *
  1192	         * <p>If the list is empty, nothing is written.
  1193	         */
  1194	        private SmithyCodeWriter writeOptionalIdList(String textBeforeList, Collection<ShapeId> shapeIds) {
  1195	            if (shapeIds.isEmpty()) {
  1196	                return this;
  1197	            }
  1198	
  1199	            openBlock("$L: [", textBeforeList);
  1200	            shapeIds.stream().sorted().forEach(shapeId -> write("$I", shapeId));
  1201	            closeBlock("]");
  1202	
  1203	            return this;
  1204	        }
  1205	
  1206	        /**
  1207	         * Formatter that quotes (and escapes) a string unless it's a valid object key string.
  1208	         */
  1209	        private String optionallyQuoteKey(Object key, String indent) {
  1210	            String formatted = AbstractCodeWriter.formatLiteral(key);
  1211	            if (UNQUOTED_KEY_STRING.matcher(formatted).matches()) {
  1212	                return formatted;
  1213	            }
  1214	            return StringUtils.escapeJavaString(formatted, indent);
  1215	        }
  1216	
  1217	        @Override
  1218	        public String toString() {
  1219	            String contents = StringUtils.stripStart(super.toString(), null);
  1220	            if (imports.isEmpty()) {
  1221	                return contents;
  1222	            }
  1223	            String importString = imports.stream()
  1224	                    .sorted()
  1225	                    .map(shapeId -> String.format("use %s", shapeId.toString()))
  1226	                    .collect(Collectors.joining("\n"));
  1227	            return importString + "\n\n" + contents;
  1228	        }
  1229	    }

- Input: `@myTrait(s: "foo.bar#Baz")` where `s` is `@idRef`
- Output: `s: Baz` (unquoted) with a `use foo.bar#Baz` import

The problem is that `foo.bar#Baz` doesn't exist as a shape in the model, so the output can't be loaded back.

So the fix should be: when the ShapeId referenced by an idRef string doesn't resolve to an actual shape in the model, we should serialize it as a quoted string rather than as an unquoted shape ID reference.

Let me look at how `formatShapeId` and `shouldWriteNamespace` work more carefully:

In `formatShapeId` (line 1143-1151):
- It converts the string to a ShapeId
- If `shouldWriteNamespace` returns false, it returns `shapeId.asRelativeReference()` (just the name)
- Otherwise it returns `shapeId.toString()` (full qualified name)

In `shouldWriteNamespace`:
- If the namespace equals the current namespace, return false (write relative)
- If it's a prelude shape, check for conflicts
- Otherwise, add to imports and return based on whether it's already imported

The problem is that for a ShapeId like `foo.bar#Baz` that doesn't exist in the model, it gets treated like a real shape: it's added to imports and rendered as just `Baz`. But when the model is loaded again, `Baz` can't be resolved.

     8	import software.amazon.smithy.model.node.Node;
     9	import software.amazon.smithy.model.node.ObjectNode;
    10	import software.amazon.smithy.model.selector.Selector;
    11	import software.amazon.smithy.model.shapes.ShapeId;
    12	import software.amazon.smithy.utils.ToSmithyBuilder;
    13	
    14	/**
    15	 * Indicates that a string value must contain a valid shape ID.
    16	 *
    17	 * <p>{@code failWhenMissing} can be set to true to fail when the
    18	 * shape ID contained in a string shape cannot be found in the result
    19	 * set of the {@code selector} property. {@code failWhenMissing} defaults to
    20	 * {@code false} when not set.
    21	 *
    22	 * <p>The {@code selector} property is used to query the model for all shapes
    23	 * that match a shape selector. The value contained within the string shape
    24	 * targeted by this trait MUST match one of the shapes returns by the shape
    25	 * selector if {@code failWhenMissing} is set to true. {@code selector}
    26	 * defaults to "*" when not set.
    27	 */
    28	public final class IdRefTrait extends AbstractTrait implements ToSmithyBuilder<IdRefTrait> {
    29	    public static final ShapeId ID = ShapeId.from("smithy.api#idRef");
    30	
    31	    private final Selector selector;
    32	    private final boolean failWhenMissing;
    33	    private final String errorMessage;
    34	
    35	    private IdRefTrait(Builder builder) {
    36	        super(ID, builder.sourceLocation);
    37	        selector = builder.selector;
    38	        failWhenMissing = builder.failWhenMissing;
    39	        errorMessage = builder.errorMessage;
    40	    }
    41	
    42	    public Selector getSelector() {
    43	        return selector == null ? Selector.IDENTITY : selector;
    44	    }
    45	
    46	    public boolean failWhenMissing() {
    47	        return failWhenMissing;
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    public Optional<String> getErrorMessage() {
    51	        return Optional.ofNullable(errorMessage);
    52	    }
    53	
    54	    @Override
    55	    public Builder toBuilder() {
    56	        return builder().sourceLocation(getSourceLocation())
    57	                .failWhenMissing(failWhenMissing)
    58	                .selector(selector)
    59	                .errorMessage(errorMessage);
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    @Override
    63	    protected Node createNode() {
    64	        ObjectNode.Builder builder = Node.objectNodeBuilder()
    65	                .sourceLocation(getSourceLocation())
    66	                .withOptionalMember(
    67	                        "selector",
    68	                        Optional.ofNullable(selector).map(Selector::toString).map(Node::from))
    69	                .withOptionalMember("errorMessage", getErrorMessage().map(Node::from));
    70	        if (failWhenMissing) {
    71	            builder = builder.withMember("failWhenMissing", Node.from(true));
    72	        }
    73	        return builder.build();
    74	    }
    75	
    76	    public static Builder builder() {
    77	        return new Builder();
    78	    }
    79	
    80	    public static final class Builder extends AbstractTraitBuilder<IdRefTrait, Builder> {
    81	        private Selector selector;
    82	        private boolean failWhenMissing;
    83	        private String errorMessage;
    84	
    85	        private Builder() {}
    86	
    87	        public Builder failWhenMissing(boolean failWhenMissing) {
    88	            this.failWhenMissing = failWhenMissing;
    89	            return this;
    90	        }
    91	
    92	        public Builder selector(Selector selector) {
    93	            this.selector = selector;
    94	            return this;
    95	        }
    96	
    97	        public Builder errorMessage(String errorMessage) {
    98	            this.errorMessage = errorMessage;
    99	            return this;
   100	        }
   101	
   102	        @Override
   103	        public IdRefTrait build() {
   104	            return new IdRefTrait(this);
   105	        }
   106	    }
   107	
   108	    public static final class Provider implements TraitService {
   109	        @Override
   110	        public ShapeId getShapeId() {
   111	            return ID;
   112	        }
   113	
   114	        @Override
   115	        public IdRefTrait createTrait(ShapeId target, Node value) {
   116	            Builder builder = builder().sourceLocation(value);
   117	            value.expectObjectNode()
   118	                    .getMember("selector", Selector::fromNode, builder::selector)
   119	                    .getBooleanMember("failWhenMissing", builder::failWhenMissing)
   120	                    .getStringMember("errorMessage", builder::errorMessage);
   121	            IdRefTrait result = builder.build();
   122	            result.setNodeCache(value);
   123	            return result;
   124	        }
   125	    }

Now I understand the issue fully. Let me look at how `serializeShapeId` should be modified. The key insight is: when we have an `@idRef` string, we should check if the ShapeId actually exists in the model. If it doesn't exist, we should serialize it as a quoted string instead of as an unquoted shape ID reference.

But wait, there's a subtlety. The `idRef` trait means "this string contains a shape ID". It doesn't mean "this shape ID must exist in the model" - that's what `failWhenMissing` controls. But the serialization shouldn't break the model.

Let me think about this more carefully:

1. When `failWhenMissing` is false, the idRef string may reference a shape that doesn't exist. That's fine.
2. But the serializer currently always renders it unquoted (like a shape reference), which means the loader will try to resolve it and fail if it doesn't exist.

The solution should be: when serializing an `@idRef` string, check if the ShapeId in the string actually resolves to a known shape in the model. If it does, serialize it as a shape ID (unquoted). If it doesn't, serialize it as a quoted string.

    48	    @TestFactory
    49	    public Stream<DynamicTest> generateTests() throws IOException, URISyntaxException {
    50	        return Files.list(Paths.get(TEST_FILE_URL.toURI()))
    51	                .map(path -> DynamicTest.dynamicTest(path.getFileName().toString(), () -> testConversion(path)));
    52	    }
    53	
    54	    public void testConversion(Path path) {
    55	        Model model = Model.assembler().addImport(path).assemble().unwrap();
    56	        SmithyIdlModelSerializer serializer = SmithyIdlModelSerializer.builder().build();
    57	        Map<Path, String> serialized = serializer.serialize(model);
    58	
    59	        if (serialized.size() != 1) {
    60	            throw new RuntimeException("Exactly one smithy file should be output for generated tests.");
    61	        }
    62	
    63	        String serializedString = serialized.entrySet().iterator().next().getValue();
    64	        assertEquals(IoUtils.readUtf8File(path).replaceAll("\\R", "\n"), serializedString);
    65	    }
    66	
    67	    @Test
    68	    public void multipleNamespacesGenerateMultipleFiles() throws Exception {
    69	        Model model = Model.assembler()
    70	                .addImport(getClass().getResource("idl-serialization/multiple-namespaces/input.json"))
    71	                .assemble()
    72	                .unwrap();
    73	        Path outputDir = Paths.get(getClass().getResource("idl-serialization/multiple-namespaces/output").toURI());
    74	        SmithyIdlModelSerializer serializer = SmithyIdlModelSerializer.builder()
    75	                .basePath(outputDir)
    76	                .build();
    77	        Map<Path, String> serialized = serializer.serialize(model);
    78	        serialized.forEach((path, generated) -> assertThat(
    79	                generated,
    80	                equalTo(IoUtils.readUtf8File(path).replaceAll("\\R", "\n"))));
    81	    }

But if the shape ID doesn\'t actually exist in the model, this causes problems.\n\nThe fix should be in `serializeShapeId` or in the `isShapeId` check: we should check if the ShapeId in the string actually resolves to a known shape in the model. }

                codeWriter.writeInline(\"\$S\", node.getValue());

        }'''

Now, an important consideration: when the `@idRef` string contains an absolute shape ID like `"foo.bar#Baz"`, `ShapeId.from` will parse it correctly. But what if it's a relative reference? That shouldn't happen because the `@idRef` trait is typically used with absolute shape IDs. But even if it does, the current code would handle it the same way.

However, there's another edge case: what if the `@idRef` string references a shape that IS in the model? In that case, our fix correctly serializes it unquoted. But what if there are multiple shapes with the same name in different namespaces? The `model.getShape(shapeId)` would find the exact one.

Let me also think about another scenario: what about the case in the PR description where `failWhenMissing` is true? In that case, if the shape doesn't exist, the model validation would fail before serialization. But if it passes (shape exists), our fix would still work correctly.

Now, there's another consideration: the `formatShapeId` method in `SmithyCodeWriter` line 1143-1151:

```java
private String formatShapeId(Object value) {
    if (value == null) {
        return "";
    }
    ShapeId shapeId = ShapeId.from(String.valueOf(value));
    if (!shouldWriteNamespace(shapeId)) {
        return shapeId.asRelativeReference();
    }
    return shapeId.toString();
}
```

This method is used by `$I` formatter. When we call `codeWriter.writeInline("$I", node.getValue())`, it eventually calls `formatShapeId` which tries to figure out whether to write the namespace or not. If the shape doesn't exist in the model but is in a different namespace, it would add it to imports and write just the name. This is the exact problem described in the PR.

Our fix prevents this by only using `$I` when the shape actually exists in the model.

But wait, there's another subtlety: what if the shape exists but in a different namespace, and the current namespace has a shape with the same name? The `shouldWriteNamespace` method handles this by checking `conflictsWithLocalNamespace`. That's fine because the shape does exist.

Now let me also think about whether we need to handle the case in `isShapeId` method too. Currently:

```java
private boolean isShapeId(Shape shape) {
    if (shape == null) {
        return false;
    }
    return shape.getMemberTrait(model, IdRefTrait.class).isPresent();
}
```

This just checks if the shape has the `@idRef` trait. Our fix in `serializeShapeId` handles the case where the shape ID doesn't exist. But what if someone has an `@idRef` string that is actually just a plain string (not a valid shape ID)? The `ShapeId.from` call would throw a `ShapeIdSyntaxException`. Let me check:

Actually, looking at the PR description, the issue is specifically about valid ShapeIds that don't resolve to existing shapes. The `@idRef` trait validates that the string is a valid ShapeId, so `ShapeId.from` should succeed. But to be safe, we might want to catch the exception. Let me check if there are any other places where `ShapeId.from` is used on the node value that could fail.

Actually, looking again at `formatShapeId` in SmithyCodeWriter (line 1147):
```java
ShapeId shapeId = ShapeId.from(String.valueOf(value));
```

If the value is not a valid ShapeId, this would throw. But since we only call `$I` when the shape exists (our fix), and the `@idRef` trait ensures the string is a valid shape ID, this should be safe.

Let me also consider: should we also handle this in the `serialize` method itself, rather than just in `serializeShapeId`? The current flow is:

1. `serialize(node, shape)` checks `isShapeId(shape)` → if true, calls `serializeShapeId`
2. `serializeShapeId` now checks if the shape exists in the model

I think this is the right place. But let me also think about whether there's an issue with the `$I` formatter and how it handles shape IDs that don't exist.

Actually, let me trace through the full scenario from the PR description more carefully:

Input model has:
- `@trait structure myTrait { @idRef @required s: String }`
- `@myTrait(s: "foo.bar#Baz") string Demo`

When serializing:
1. The trait `myTrait` is serialized. For the member `s`, it has `@idRef`, so `isShapeId` returns true.
2. `serializeShapeId` is called with `StringNode("foo.bar#Baz")`.
3. With our fix: `ShapeId.from("foo.bar#Baz")` creates `ShapeId("foo.bar", "Baz")`.
4. `model.getShape(shapeId)` returns `Optional.empty()` because `foo.bar#Baz` doesn't exist in the model.
5. So we call `codeWriter.writeInline("$S", "foo.bar#Baz")` which writes `"foo.bar#Baz"` (quoted).

This matches the expected behavior: the output should be `s: "foo.bar#Baz"` (quoted), not `s: Baz` (unquoted).

    ShapeId shapeId = ShapeId.from(String.valueOf(value));
    if (!shouldWriteNamespace(shapeId)) {
        return shapeId.asRelativeReference();

   415	        ShapeIdFactory() {
   416	            preludeCache = new ConcurrentHashMap<>(PRELUDE_MAX_SIZE);
   417	
   418	            // A simple LRU cache based on LinkedHashMap, wrapped in a synchronized map.
   419	            nonPreludeCache = Collections.synchronizedMap(new LinkedHashMap<String, ShapeId>(

   423	                @Override

   426	                }
   427	            });

   429	
   430	        ShapeId create(final String key) {
   431	            if (key.startsWith(PRELUDE_PREFIX)) {
   432	                return getPreludeId(key);
   433	            } else {
   434	                return getNonPreludeId(key);
   435	            }
   436	        }
   437	
   438	        private ShapeId getPreludeId(String key) {
   439	            // computeIfAbsent isn't used here since we need to limit the cache size and creating multiple IDs
   440	            // simultaneously isn't an issue.
   441	            ShapeId result = preludeCache.get(key);
   442	            if (result != null) {
   443	                return result;
   444	            }
   445	
   446	            // The ID wasn't found so build it, and add it to the cache if the cache isn't too big already.
   447	            result = buildShapeId(key);
   448	
   449	            if (preludeCache.size() <= PRELUDE_MAX_SIZE) {
   450	                preludeCache.putIfAbsent(key, result);
   451	            }
   452	
   453	            return result;
   454	        }
   455	
   456	        private ShapeId getNonPreludeId(String key) {
   457	            return nonPreludeCache.computeIfAbsent(key, ShapeIdFactory::buildShapeId);
   458	        }

2026-05-30 01:49:21,475 - INFO - swea-agent-smithy-lang__smithy-3038 - 💭 THOUGHT
The code looks good. But I'm now thinking about whether there's a better approach. Let me re-read the PR description:

> `SmithyIdlSerializer` always renders idRefs unquoted

The issue is that idRef strings are always rendered unquoted (as shape IDs), which causes problems when the shape doesn't exist in the model.

My fix checks if the shape exists in the model. If it does, render unquoted; if not, render quoted.

But there's another consideration: what about the case where the shape exists but `failWhenMissing` is false? In that case, the `@idRef` trait allows the string to reference a shape that may or may not exist. But if it does exist, rendering it unquoted is fine.

What about the case where `failWhenMissing` is true? In that case, the model validation would have already ensured the shape exists. So if we're serializing a validated model, the shape should exist. But if someone serializes an unvalidated model... well, the model should be valid before serialization.

I think my fix is correct. Let me also check if there's a possibility where the shape exists but should still be quoted (e.g., when the shape is in the same namespace and the name conflicts with something else). Actually, if the shape exists, it should always be fine to render it unquoted because the `$I` formatter handles imports and namespace resolution correctly.

Now let me check if there are any other places in the code that might have similar issues. Let me search for patterns like `$I` used with idRef or similar:

🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/TestIdRefFix.java << 'EOF'
import software.amazon.smithy.model.Model;
import software.amazon.smithy.model.shapes.SmithyIdlModelSerializer;
import java.util.Map;
import java.nio.file.Path;

public class TestIdRefFix {
    public static void main(String[] args) {
        // Test 1: idRef to non-existent shape should be serialized quoted
        Model model1 = Model.assembler()
            .addUnparsedModel(
                "test.smithy",
                "$version: \"2\"\n"
                + "namespace test\n"
                + "\n"
                + "@trait structure myTrait { @idRef @required s: String }\n"
                + "\n"
                + "@myTrait(s: \"foo.bar#Baz\")\n"
                + "string Demo\n"
            )
            .assemble()
            .unwrap();

        SmithyIdlModelSerializer serializer = SmithyIdlModelSerializer.builder().build();
        Map<Path, String> serialized = serializer.serialize(model1);
        String result = serialized.values().iterator().next();
        
        System.out.println("=== Test 1: Non-existent shape referenced by idRef ===");
        System.out.println(result);
        System.out.println();
        
        if (result.contains("\"foo.bar#Baz\"")) {
            System.out.println("PASS: idRef to non-existent shape is quoted");
        } else if (result.contains("foo.bar#Baz")) {
            System.out.println("PASS: idRef to non-existent shape uses absolute ID");
        } else if (result.contains("use foo.bar#Baz") && result.contains("Baz")) {
            System.out.println("FAIL: idRef to non-existent shape is unquoted with import (would break reload)");
        } else {
            System.out.println("UNKNOWN: " + result);
        }
        
        // Test that the serialized model can be loaded again
        try {
            Model model2 = Model.assembler()
                .addUnparsedModel("test.smithy", result)
                .assemble()
                .unwrap();
            System.out.println("PASS: Serialized model can be loaded again");
        } catch (Exception e) {
            System.out.println("FAIL: Serialized model cannot be loaded: " + e.getMessage());
        }
        
        System.out.println();
        
        // Test 2: idRef to existing shape should still be serialized unquoted
        Model model2 = Model.assembler()
            .addUnparsedModel(
                "test.smithy",
                "$version: \"2\"\n"
                + "namespace test\n"
                + "\n"
                + "@trait structure myTrait { @idRef @required s: String }\n"
                + "\n"
                + "string Baz\n"
                + "\n"
                + "@myTrait(s: \"test#Baz\")\n"
                + "string Demo\n"
            )
            .assemble()
            .unwrap();

        Map<Path, String> serialized2 = serializer.serialize(model2);
        String result2 = serialized2.values().iterator().next();
        
        System.out.println("=== Test 2: Existing shape referenced by idRef ===");
        System.out.println(result2);
        System.out.println();
        
        if (result2.contains("\"test#Baz\"")) {
            System.out.println("INFO: idRef to existing shape is quoted (still valid)");
        } else if (result2.contains("Baz") && !result2.contains("\"test#Baz\"")) {
            System.out.println("PASS: idRef to existing shape is unquoted");
        }
        
        // Test that the serialized model can be loaded again
        try {
            Model model2b = Model.assembler()
                .addUnparsedModel("test.smithy", result2)
                .assemble()
                .unwrap();
            System.out.println("PASS: Serialized model can be loaded again");
        } catch (Exception e) {
            System.out.println("FAIL: Serialized model cannot be loaded: " + e.getMessage());
        }
    }
}
EOF

Both tests pass:

1. **Test 1 (non-existent shape)**: `"foo.bar#Baz"` is now quoted, and the serialized model can be loaded again. Before the fix, this would have been rendered as `Baz` with a `use foo.bar#Baz` import, which would fail on reload.

2. **Test 2 (existing shape)**: `test#Baz` is rendered as just `Baz` (unquoted, since it's in the same namespace), and the serialized model can be loaded again. This preserves the original behavior for existing shapes.

The fix works correctly!

Let me also think about edge cases I might have missed:

1. **Shape exists in a different namespace**: If we have `@myTrait(s: "other.ns#Baz")` and `other.ns#Baz` exists in the model, our fix will serialize it as `Baz` with a `use other.ns#Baz` import. That's correct.

2. **Shape with `failWhenMissing: true`**: If the idRef has `failWhenMissing: true`, the shape must exist. Our fix handles this correctly because the shape will exist in the model.

3. **idRef on a list of strings**: What if we have a list of idRef strings? The `serializeArray` method calls `serialize(element, member)` for each element, which goes through the same `isShapeId` check and then `serializeShapeId`. So our fix handles this case too.

4. **idRef in nested structures**: If a structure has a member that is another structure, and that inner structure has an idRef member, the serialization goes through `serializeKeyValuePairs` → `serialize(value, member)` → `isShapeId(shape)` → `serializeShapeId`. Our fix handles this.

I believe the fix is complete and correct. Let me do a final check on the modified file to ensure everything looks good:
